class="infobox-label">Gates</th><td class="infobox-data">115 (in terminal)</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Sources: UK <a href="/wiki/Aeronautical_Information_Publication" title="Aeronautical Information Publication">AIP</a> at <a href="/wiki/National_Air_Traffic_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="National Air Traffic Services">NATS</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aip_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Statistics from CAA.</div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Gatwick Airport</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/\xc9\xa1/: &#39;g&#39; in &#39;guy&#39;">\xc9\xa1</span><span title="/\xc3\xa6/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">\xc3\xa6</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="&#39;w&#39; in &#39;wind&#39;">w</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span></span>/</a></span></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> also known as <b>London Gatwick</b><sup id="cite_ref-aip_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>LGW</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>EGKK</b>), is a major international airport near <a href="/wiki/Crawley" title="Crawley">Crawley</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Sussex" title="West Sussex">West Sussex</a>, England, 29.5 miles (47.5&#160;km) south of <a href="/wiki/Central_London" title="Central London">Central London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aip_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> It is the second-busiest airport by <a href="/wiki/Busiest_airports_in_the_United_Kingdom_by_total_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="Busiest airports in the United Kingdom by total passenger traffic">total passenger traffic</a> in the UK, after <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Gatwick is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">tenth-busiest</a> airport in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>. It covers a total area of 674 hectares (1,670 acres).<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gatwick opened as an aerodrome in the late 1920s; it has been in use for commercial flights since 1933. The airport has two terminals, the North Terminal and the South Terminal, which cover areas of 98,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (117,000&#160;sq&#160;yd) and 160,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (190,000&#160;sq&#160;yd) respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> It operates as a single-runway airport, using a main runway with a length of 3,316&#160;m (10,879&#160;ft). A secondary runway is available but, due to its proximity to the main runway, can only be used if the main runway is not in use. In 2018, 46.1&#160;million passengers passed through the airport, a 1.1% increase compared with 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-LGW_2018_GAL_Stats_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGW_2018_GAL_Stats-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" class="toctext">Ground transport</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Road"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Road</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Rail"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Rail</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Bus"><span class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Citations"><span class="tocnumber">12.1</span> <span class="toctext">Citations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">12.2</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Gatwick_Airport" title="Timeline of Gatwick Airport">Timeline of Gatwick Airport</a></div>\n<p>The land on which Gatwick Airport stands was first developed as an <a href="/wiki/Aerodrome" title="Aerodrome">aerodrome</a> in the late 1920s. The <a href="/wiki/Air_Ministry" title="Air Ministry">Air Ministry</a> approved commercial flights from the site in 1933, and the first terminal, "<a href="/wiki/Beehive,_Gatwick_Airport" title="Beehive, Gatwick Airport">The Beehive</a>", was built in 1935. Scheduled air services from the new terminal began the following year. Major development work at the airport took place during the 1950s. The airport buildings were designed by <a href="/wiki/Yorke_Rosenberg_Mardall" title="Yorke Rosenberg Mardall">Yorke Rosenberg Mardall</a> between 1955 and 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gatwick_Airport,_1970a_geograph-3212288-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Gatwick_Airport%2C_1970a_geograph-3212288-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg/220px-Gatwick_Airport%2C_1970a_geograph-3212288-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Gatwick_Airport%2C_1970a_geograph-3212288-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg/330px-Gatwick_Airport%2C_1970a_geograph-3212288-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Gatwick_Airport%2C_1970a_geograph-3212288-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg/440px-Gatwick_Airport%2C_1970a_geograph-3212288-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1156" data-file-height="690" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gatwick_Airport,_1970a_geograph-3212288-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gatwick Airport in 1970</div></div></div>\n<p>In the 1960s, <a href="/wiki/British_United_Airways" title="British United Airways">British United Airways</a> (BUA) and <a href="/wiki/Dan-Air" title="Dan-Air">Dan-Air</a> were two of the largest British independent<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;nb 2&#93;</a></sup> airlines at Gatwick, with the former establishing itself as the dominant scheduled operator at the airport as well as providing a significant number of the airport\'s non-scheduled services and the latter becoming its leading provider of <a href="/wiki/Package_tour" title="Package tour">inclusive tour</a> charter services.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Further rapid growth of charter flights at Gatwick was encouraged by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Aviation" title="Ministry of Aviation">Ministry of Aviation</a>, which instructed airlines to move regular charter flights from Heathrow. Following the takeover of BUA by <a href="/wiki/Caledonian_Airways" title="Caledonian Airways">Caledonian Airways</a> at the beginning of the following decade, the resulting airline, <a href="/wiki/British_Caledonian" title="British Caledonian">British Caledonian</a> (BCal), became Gatwick\'s dominant scheduled airline during the 1970s. While continuing to dominate scheduled operations at Gatwick for most of the 1980s, BCal was also one of the airport\'s major charter airlines until the end of the 1970s (together with Dan-Air, <a href="/wiki/Laker_Airways" title="Laker Airways">Laker Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Airtours" title="British Airtours">British Airtours</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-..._Bloomers_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-..._Bloomers-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> As a result of conditions imposed by Britain\'s <a href="/wiki/Competition_Commission" title="Competition Commission">Monopolies and Mergers Commission</a> on the takeover of BCal by the then newly privatised <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> (BA) at the end of the 1980s, Dan-Air and <a href="/wiki/Air_Europe" title="Air Europe">Air Europe</a> assumed BCal\'s former role as Gatwick\'s dominant scheduled short-haul operator while BA continued in BCal\'s erstwhile role as the airport\'s most important scheduled long-haul operator. Following the demise of Air Europe and Dan-Air (both of which had continued to provide a significant number of charter flights in addition to a growing number of scheduled short-haul flights at Gatwick) in the early 1990s, BA began building up Gatwick into a secondary <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">hub</a> (complementing its main hub at Heathrow). These moves resulted in BA becoming Gatwick\'s dominant airline by the turn of the millennium.<sup id="cite_ref-..._up_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-..._up-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> BA\'s subsequent decision to de-hub Gatwick provided the space for <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a> to establish its biggest base at the airport and to become its dominant airline.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/BAA_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="BAA Limited">BAA Limited</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport_Holdings" title="Heathrow Airport Holdings">Heathrow Airport Holdings Limited</a>) and its predecessors, BAA plc and the British Airports Authority, owned and operated Gatwick from 1 April 1966 to 2 December 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 1978 to 2008, many flights to and from the United States used Gatwick because of restrictions on the use of Heathrow implemented in the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_II_Agreement" title="Bermuda II Agreement">Bermuda II agreement</a> between the UK and the US.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/US_Airways" title="US Airways">US Airways</a>, Gatwick\'s last remaining US carrier, ended its service between Gatwick and <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Douglas_International_Airport" title="Charlotte Douglas International Airport">Charlotte</a> on 30 March 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-US_LGWFinal_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_LGWFinal-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> This left Gatwick without a scheduled US airline for the first time in 35 years.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Prior to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a> announced its intent to launch service between Gatwick and <a href="/wiki/Logan_International_Airport" title="Logan International Airport">Logan International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a> in summer 2020, which would have made it the first US airline to service Gatwick since the withdrawal of the US Airways service in 2013, but the massive global travel downturn placed these plans on indefinite hold.<sup id="cite_ref-DeltaVirgin_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeltaVirgin-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 17 September 2008, BAA announced it would sell Gatwick after the <a href="/wiki/Competition_Commission" title="Competition Commission">Competition Commission</a> published a report about BAA\'s market dominance in London and the <a href="/wiki/South_East_England" title="South East England">South East</a>. On 21 October 2009, it was announced that an agreement had been reached to sell Gatwick to a consortium led by <a href="/wiki/Global_Infrastructure_Partners" title="Global Infrastructure Partners">Global Infrastructure Partners</a> (GIP), who also have a <a href="/wiki/Controlling_interest" title="Controlling interest">controlling interest</a> in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Airport" title="Edinburgh Airport">Edinburgh</a><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;nb 3&#93;</a></sup> airport, for \xc2\xa31.51&#160;billion. The sale was completed on 3 December.<sup id="cite_ref-Sale_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sale-24">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In February 2010, GIP sold minority stakes in the airport of 12% and 15% to the South Korean National Pension Service and the Abu Dhabi Investment Authority (ADIA) for \xc2\xa3100&#160;million and \xc2\xa3125&#160;million, respectively. The sales were part of GIP\'s <a href="/wiki/Strategic_management" title="Strategic management">strategy</a> to <a href="/wiki/Syndicate#Finance" title="Syndicate">syndicate</a> the <a href="/wiki/Equity_(finance)" title="Equity (finance)">equity</a> portion of the original acquisition by issuing <a href="/wiki/Bond_(finance)" title="Bond (finance)">bonds</a> to <a href="/wiki/Refinancing" title="Refinancing">refinance</a> bank debt. Although this entails bringing additional investors into the airport, GIP aims to retain <a href="/wiki/Control_(management)" title="Control (management)">management control</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gatwick_AdditionalInvestors_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gatwick_AdditionalInvestors-25">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gatwick_Securitisation_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gatwick_Securitisation-26">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">Californian</a> state pension fund <a href="/wiki/CalPERS" title="CalPERS">CalPERS</a> acquired a 12.7% stake in Gatwick Airport for about $155&#160;million (\xc2\xa3104.8&#160;million) in June 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-CalPERS1_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CalPERS1-27">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> On 21 December 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Australian_dollar" title="Australian dollar">A$</a>69&#160;billion (\xc2\xa344&#160;billion) Future Fund, a sovereign wealth fund established by the Australian government in 2006, agreed to purchase a 17.2% stake in Gatwick Airport from GIP for \xc2\xa3145&#160;million. This transaction completed GIP\'s syndication process for the airport, reducing its stake to 42% (although the firm\'s extra <a href="/wiki/Voting_interest" title="Voting interest">voting rights</a> meant it still controlled the airport\'s <a href="/wiki/Board_of_directors" title="Board of directors">board</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-FutureFund_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FutureFund-28">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2020, the airport announced that has plans to cut over a quarter of its employees as a result of a planned company restructuring caused by the effects of the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>. The planned cuts will bring the total workforce of the airport to 1,900; before the start of the pandemic it was 3,300, however, additional 785 jobs were cut earlier in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership">Ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Ownership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The airport is owned and operated by Gatwick Airport Limited, a wholly owned subsidiary of Ivy Holdco Limited,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> owned by <a href="/wiki/Global_Infrastructure_Partners" title="Global Infrastructure Partners">Global Infrastructure Partners</a> (GIP), among others.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In December 2018, <a href="/wiki/Vinci_SA" title="Vinci SA">Vinci</a> announced that it would acquire 50.01% majority stake for \xc2\xa32.9bn, with a GIP-managed consortium of investors (Abu Dhabi Investment Authority, Australia\'s sovereign wealth fund and two public pension funds in California and South Korea) owning the remaining 49.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The sale was completed by the middle of 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EGKK_Layout.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/EGKK_Layout.svg/220px-EGKK_Layout.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/EGKK_Layout.svg/330px-EGKK_Layout.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/EGKK_Layout.svg/440px-EGKK_Layout.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1063" data-file-height="1063" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EGKK_Layout.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Airport Map (as of November 2016)</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 31 May 2008, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Holidays" title="Virgin Holidays">Virgin Holidays</a> opened the V Room, Gatwick\'s first lounge dedicated to their long-haul leisure travellers. On 25 January 2017, the lounge moved to the North Terminal together with the Virgin Atlantic Clubhouse as part of the airline moves that saw British Airways and Virgin Atlantic exchange their previous terminal locations and EasyJet consolidated in the North Terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> On 9 April 2009, an independent pay-for-access lounge opened in the South Terminal. Gatwick also has a conference and business centre, and several on- and off-site hotels ranging in class from executive to <a href="/wiki/Capsule_hotel" title="Capsule hotel">economy</a>.\n</p><p>The airport has <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglican</a>, Catholic and <a href="/wiki/Free_Church_of_England" title="Free Church of England">Free Church</a> chaplains, and there are <a href="/wiki/Multifaith_space" title="Multifaith space">multi-faith prayer</a> and counselling rooms in each terminal. A daily service is led by one of the chaplains.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Aviation Authority (United Kingdom)">Civil Aviation Authority</a> Safety Regulation Group is in Aviation House.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/WesternGeco" title="WesternGeco">WesternGeco</a>, a geophysical services company, has its head office and Europe\xe2\x80\x93Africa\xe2\x80\x93Russia offices in Schlumberger House,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> a 124,000&#160;sq&#160;ft (11,500&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) building on the airport grounds<sup id="cite_ref-Eade_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eade-41">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> near the South Terminal. The company had a 15-year lease on the building, scheduled to expire in June 2008. In 2007, WesternGeco reached an agreement with its landlord, BAA Lynton, extending its lease to 2016 at an initial rent of \xc2\xa32.1&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-Eade_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eade-41">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fastjet" title="Fastjet">Fastjet</a> has its <a href="/wiki/Registered_office" title="Registered office">registered</a> and head offices at Suite 2C in First Point at the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Before the sale, BAA planned an \xc2\xa3874&#160;million investment at Gatwick over five years, including increased capacity for both terminals, improvements to transport interchange and a new baggage system for the South Terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Passengers passing through the airport are informed about the redevelopment programme with large <a href="/wiki/QR_code" title="QR code">mobile barcodes</a> on top of construction hoardings. Scanning these transfers information on the construction to the user\'s <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In summer 2013, Gatwick introduced Gatwick Connect, a free flight connection service to assist passengers changing flights at Gatwick whose airlines do not provide a full flight connection service. On 15 September 2015, the service was rebranded as "GatwickConnects".<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LGW_1st_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGW_1st-46">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> It is available to passengers connecting on several major airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flight_movements">Flight movements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Flight movements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gatwick_Air_Traffic_Control_tower_-_geograph.org.uk_-_237405.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Tall, white control tower" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Gatwick_Air_Traffic_Control_tower_-_geograph.org.uk_-_237405.jpg/220px-Gatwick_Air_Traffic_Control_tower_-_geograph.org.uk_-_237405.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Gatwick_Air_Traffic_Control_tower_-_geograph.org.uk_-_237405.jpg/330px-Gatwick_Air_Traffic_Control_tower_-_geograph.org.uk_-_237405.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Gatwick_Air_Traffic_Control_tower_-_geograph.org.uk_-_237405.jpg/440px-Gatwick_Air_Traffic_Control_tower_-_geograph.org.uk_-_237405.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="547" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gatwick_Air_Traffic_Control_tower_-_geograph.org.uk_-_237405.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The airport control tower opened in 1984.</div></div></div>\n<p>Gatwick operates as a single-runway airport although it has two runways; the northern runway (08L/26R) can only be used when the main runway (08R/26L) is out of use for any reason. The UK Integrated Aeronautical Information Package gives the Takeoff Run Available (TORA) of its main runway (08R/26L) as 3,255 m when aircraft take off in a westerly direction (26) and 3,159 m when takeoffs occur in an easterly direction (08). The documentation lists the respective TORA for the northern runway (08L/26R) as 2,565 m in both directions. Nearly three-quarters of takeoffs are towards the west (74% over a 12-month period). Both runways are 148&#160;ft (45&#160;m) wide; they are 656&#160;ft (200&#160;m) apart,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> which is insufficient for the simultaneous use of both runways. During normal operations the northern runway is used as a taxiway,<sup id="cite_ref-runway_moratorium_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-runway_moratorium-52">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-1979_expansion_plans_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1979_expansion_plans-53">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> consistent with its original construction (although it was gradually widened).<sup id="cite_ref-LGW_History_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGW_History-54">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2018, the airport announced that it was "exploring how to make best use of its existing runways, including the possibility of bringing its existing standby runway into routine use".<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> One scenario would see 08L/26R used for departing narrow-body aircraft only, while the longer 08R/26L would be used for wide-body take-offs and all landings; widening 08L/26R would also increase the centreline separation slightly. New technology could also be used to increase capacity on the main runway, and in the longer term the airport remains interested in constructing a new runway to the south.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The main runway uses a Category III <a href="/wiki/Instrument_Landing_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Instrument Landing System">Instrument Landing System</a> (ILS). The northern runway does not have an ILS; when it is in use, arriving aircraft use a combination of <a href="/wiki/Distance_measuring_equipment" class="mw-redirect" title="Distance measuring equipment">distance measuring equipment</a> and assistance from the approach controller (using surveillance radar) or (where equipped, and subject to operator approval) an RNAV (<a href="/wiki/Global_navigation_satellite_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Global navigation satellite system">GNSS</a>) approach (also available for the main runway).<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> On both runways, a <a href="/wiki/Continuous_descent_approach" title="Continuous descent approach">continuous descent approach</a> is used to minimise the environmental effects of incoming aircraft, particularly at night.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Night flights are subject to restrictions;<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> between 11&#160;pm and 7&#160;am, noisier aircraft (rated <a href="/wiki/Quota_Count_system" title="Quota Count system">QC</a>/8 and QC/16) may not operate. From 11.30&#160;pm to 6&#160;am (the night quota period) there are three limits: Number of flights, a <a href="/wiki/Quota_Count_system" title="Quota Count system">Quota Count system</a>, limiting total noise permitted<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> and no night <a href="/wiki/Night_flying_restrictions" title="Night flying restrictions">QC/4</a> flights.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Security">Security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport is policed by the Gatwick District of <a href="/wiki/Sussex_Police" title="Sussex Police">Sussex Police</a>. The district is responsible for the entire airport (including aircraft) and, in certain circumstances, aircraft in flight. The 150 officers attached to this district include armed and unarmed officers, and <a href="/wiki/Police_Community_Support_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Police Community Support Officer">community support officers</a> for minor offences. The airport district counters <a href="/wiki/Man-portable_air-defense_systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Man-portable air-defense systems">man-portable surface-to-air missiles</a> (MANPADS) by patrolling in and around the airport and a separate sub-unit has vehicle checks around the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Access to airside portions of the airport is controlled and maintained by the airport\'s team of security officers, regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a>. <a href="/wiki/Brook_House_Immigration_Removal_Centre" title="Brook House Immigration Removal Centre">Brook House</a>, an immigration-removal centre of <a href="/wiki/Immigration_Enforcement" title="Immigration Enforcement">Immigration Enforcement</a>, was opened near the airport on 18 March 2009 by the then <a href="/wiki/Home_Secretary" title="Home Secretary">Home Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/Jacqui_Smith" title="Jacqui Smith">Jacqui Smith</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_airlines">Major airlines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Major airlines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Welcome_To_The_North_Terminal_-_geograph.org.uk_-_775980.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Welcome_To_The_North_Terminal_-_geograph.org.uk_-_775980.jpg/220px-Welcome_To_The_North_Terminal_-_geograph.org.uk_-_775980.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Welcome_To_The_North_Terminal_-_geograph.org.uk_-_775980.jpg/330px-Welcome_To_The_North_Terminal_-_geograph.org.uk_-_775980.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Welcome_To_The_North_Terminal_-_geograph.org.uk_-_775980.jpg/440px-Welcome_To_The_North_Terminal_-_geograph.org.uk_-_775980.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="452" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Welcome_To_The_North_Terminal_-_geograph.org.uk_-_775980.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Exterior of the North Terminal before renovation</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gatwick_Airport,_North_Terminal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Gatwick_Airport%2C_North_Terminal.jpg/220px-Gatwick_Airport%2C_North_Terminal.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Gatwick_Airport%2C_North_Terminal.jpg/330px-Gatwick_Airport%2C_North_Terminal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Gatwick_Airport%2C_North_Terminal.jpg/440px-Gatwick_Airport%2C_North_Terminal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gatwick_Airport,_North_Terminal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aircraft stands at the North Terminal</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bridge_to_Pier_6,_Gatwick_North_Terminal_-_geograph.org.uk_-_74055.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Bridge_to_Pier_6%2C_Gatwick_North_Terminal_-_geograph.org.uk_-_74055.jpg/220px-Bridge_to_Pier_6%2C_Gatwick_North_Terminal_-_geograph.org.uk_-_74055.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Bridge_to_Pier_6%2C_Gatwick_North_Terminal_-_geograph.org.uk_-_74055.jpg/330px-Bridge_to_Pier_6%2C_Gatwick_North_Terminal_-_geograph.org.uk_-_74055.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Bridge_to_Pier_6%2C_Gatwick_North_Terminal_-_geograph.org.uk_-_74055.jpg/440px-Bridge_to_Pier_6%2C_Gatwick_North_Terminal_-_geograph.org.uk_-_74055.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="478" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bridge_to_Pier_6,_Gatwick_North_Terminal_-_geograph.org.uk_-_74055.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The bridge connecting the North Terminal to its apron pier</div></div></div>\n<p>The airport is a base for scheduled airlines <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> (BA), <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a>, and charter operators such as <a href="/wiki/TUI_Airways" title="TUI Airways">TUI Airways</a>. Gatwick is unique amongst London\'s airports in its representation of the three main airline business models: full service, <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost</a> and <a href="/wiki/Air_charter" title="Air charter">charter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> As of October 2016, these respectively accounted for 26.6%,<sup id="cite_ref-UKRegions_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UKRegions-64">&#91;nb 4&#93;</a></sup> 61.3%<sup id="cite_ref-UKRegions_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UKRegions-64">&#91;nb 4&#93;</a></sup> and 13.1%<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;nb 5&#93;</a></sup> of Gatwick\'s seat capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-CAPA_AirportHub_Analysis_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CAPA_AirportHub_Analysis-66">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By late 2015, <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a> flew over 100 routes from Gatwick with a fleet of more than 60 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EZY_LGW_TerminalConsolidation_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EZY_LGW_TerminalConsolidation-68">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The airport is the carrier\'s largest base, and its 16&#160;million passengers per year accounted for 45% of Gatwick\'s 2013 total<sup id="cite_ref-EZY_LGW_Takeover_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EZY_LGW_Takeover-69">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> (ahead of Gatwick\'s second-largest passenger airline: BA, whose 4.5&#160;million passengers comprised 14% of total passenger traffic in 2011\xe2\x80\x9312).<sup id="cite_ref-FY11_12_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FY11_12-70">&#91;nb 6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>EasyJet, BA and <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air_Shuttle" title="Norwegian Air Shuttle">Norwegian</a> are Gatwick\'s three biggest resident airlines. According to data from Airport Coordination Limited, these three airlines respectively accounted for 43.3%, 19% and 10.5% of <a href="/wiki/Airport_slots" class="mw-redirect" title="Airport slots">airport slots</a> in April 2018. According to this data, by April 2018 Norwegian had overtaken <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">Virgin Atlantic</a> as Gatwick\'s number one <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_flight" title="Transatlantic flight">transatlantic</a> airline by seat capacity, and BA\'s competitive response to Norwegian\'s growing commercial threat to its transatlantic business would result in Virgin\'s relegation to third position among the airport\'s transatlantic airlines during the 2018 summer timetable period.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> EasyJet, BA and Norwegian collectively accounted for 65.43% of Gatwick\'s total passengers in 2016 (EasyJet: 40.37% / 17.4&#160;million; BA: 14.39% / 6.2&#160;million; Norwegian: 10.67% / 4.6&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-LGW_Nos_2016_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGW_Nos_2016-74">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NUK_LGWSIN_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NUK_LGWSIN-76">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> As per <a href="/wiki/Official_Airline_Guide" class="mw-redirect" title="Official Airline Guide">Official Airline Guide</a> (OAG) data for the week of 29 May 2017, their respective international departure seat capacity shares at the airport for summer 2017 are: 42.1%, 15.4% and 9.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In terms of passengers carried, EasyJet and BA were also among the five largest airlines operating at Gatwick in 2010 (which also included <a href="/wiki/TUI_Airways" title="TUI Airways">TUI Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook_Airlines" title="Thomas Cook Airlines">Thomas Cook Airlines</a> at the time) and the top 10 in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LGW_1st_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGW_1st-46">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In terms of total scheduled airline seats at Gatwick in 2014, EasyJet accounted for 18.36&#160;million, more than two-and-a-half times as many as second-placed BA (seven&#160;million) and nearly five times the number offered by third-placed Norwegian Air Shuttle (3.74&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Using data sourced from the <a href="/wiki/Official_Airline_Guide" class="mw-redirect" title="Official Airline Guide">OAG Schedules Analyser</a>, the following changes in the respective departure seat capacity shares of Gatwick\'s three biggest airlines occurred from 2010 to 2015: EasyJet\'s share increased from 26.1% in 2010 to 42.1% in 2015; BA\'s share dropped from 18.3% in 2010 to 15% in 2015; Norwegian\'s share rose almost three-fold from less than 3% in 2010 to 8.3% in 2015. EasyJet, BA, Norwegian, TUI Airways, <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook_Airlines" title="Thomas Cook Airlines">Thomas Cook Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarch_Airlines" title="Monarch Airlines">Monarch Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">Virgin Atlantic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vueling" title="Vueling">Vueling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a> were Gatwick\'s top 10 airlines by share of passengers in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>EasyJet\'s acquisition of BA franchise carrier <a href="/wiki/GB_Airways" title="GB Airways">GB Airways</a> in March 2008 increased its share of airport slots to 24% (from 17% in late 2007); the airline became the largest short-haul operator at the airport, accounting for 29% of short-haul passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> By 2009, BA\'s share of Gatwick slots had fallen to 20% from its peak of 40% in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-Aer_Lingus_base_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aer_Lingus_base-82">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> By 2010, this had declined to 16%.<sup id="cite_ref-CAPA_IAG_Analysis_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CAPA_IAG_Analysis-83">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EZY_LGW_LTN_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EZY_LGW_LTN-84">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> By mid-2012, EasyJet had 45% of Gatwick\'s early-morning peak time slots (6 am to 8:55&#160;am).<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;nb 7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By 2008, <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">Flybe</a> was Gatwick\'s third-largest airline (accounting for 9% of its slots) and its fastest-growing airline.<sup id="cite_ref-Aer_Lingus_base_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aer_Lingus_base-82">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> It became the airport\'s largest domestic operator, carrying 1.2&#160;million passengers in its 2011\xe2\x80\x9312 financial year on eight routes to destinations in the UK, the Channel Islands and the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FY11_12_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FY11_12-70">&#91;nb 6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In March 2013, the airline announced that it would end operations at Gatwick, citing unsustainably high airport charges and increases in UK <a href="/wiki/Air_Passenger_Duty" title="Air Passenger Duty">Air Passenger Duty</a>. Flybe sold its 25 pairs of daily slots<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;nb 8&#93;</a></sup> at the airport to EasyJet for \xc2\xa320&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-BE_LGW_OpsCessation_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BE_LGW_OpsCessation-90">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The latter\'s share of Gatwick slots increased to 44% in summer 2014; second-placed BA has held about 16% of the airport\'s slots since 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-CAPA_IAG_Analysis_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CAPA_IAG_Analysis-83">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EZY_LGW_LTN_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EZY_LGW_LTN-84">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LGW_SlotMachine_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGW_SlotMachine-92">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Following the sale of its Gatwick slots to EasyJet, Flybe continued to provide the scheduled service between Gatwick and <a href="/wiki/Newquay" title="Newquay">Newquay</a>, as a result of being awarded the contract to fly this route under a four-year <a href="/wiki/Public_Service_Obligation" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Service Obligation">Public Service Obligation</a> (PSO), until the flight was subsequently moved from Gatwick to <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a> in April 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/EU%E2%80%93US_Open_Skies_Agreement" title="EU\xe2\x80\x93US Open Skies Agreement">EU\xe2\x80\x93US Open Skies Agreement</a>, which became effective on 30 March 2008, led a number of airlines to downsize their transatlantic operations at Gatwick in favour of Heathrow. <a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines" title="Continental Airlines">Continental Airlines</a> was the second transatlantic carrier (after <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> to leave Gatwick after its decision to transfer the seasonal <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a> service to Heathrow on 3 May 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Slots left by the US carriers (and the collapse of <a href="/wiki/Zoom_Airlines" title="Zoom Airlines">Zoom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oasis_Hong_Kong_Airlines" title="Oasis Hong Kong Airlines">Oasis Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/XL_Airways_UK" title="XL Airways UK">Excel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sterling_Airlines" title="Sterling Airlines">Sterling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook_Airlines" title="Thomas Cook Airlines">Thomas Cook</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Adria_Airways" title="Adria Airways">Adria</a>) were taken by EasyJet, <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">Flybe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air_Shuttle" title="Norwegian Air Shuttle">Norwegian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>. A number of full-service airlines have established or resumed operations at the airport, including <a href="/wiki/China_Eastern_Airlines" title="China Eastern Airlines">China Eastern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">Qatar Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">Turkish Airlines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/WestJet" title="WestJet">WestJet</a>. This is part of the airport\'s strategy to attract higher-spending <a href="/wiki/Business_travel" title="Business travel">business travellers</a> (countering its dependence on European low-cost and charter markets), increasing year-round <a href="/wiki/Capacity_utilization" title="Capacity utilization">capacity utilisation</a> by smoothing peaks and troughs in traffic. Gatwick\'s success in persuading these airlines to launch (or re-launch) routes to overseas destinations important for business and <a href="/wiki/Tourism#Leisure_travel" title="Tourism">leisure travel</a> was aided by a lack of comparable slots at Heathrow.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 5 May 2020, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">Virgin Atlantic</a> announced it was to cease operations at Gatwick due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> <sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 18 August 2020, <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">WizzAir</a> announced a new hub at Gatwick Airport. Initially basing their A321 aircraft there along with additional commercial routes to Greece, Italy, Spain, and Malta operating from October 22, 2020 onwards.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_Place_Gatwick">City Place Gatwick</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: City Place Gatwick">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/City_Place_Gatwick" title="City Place Gatwick">City Place Gatwick</a></div>\n<p>Gatwick\'s original terminal, the Beehive, is included within the City Place Gatwick office complex together with 1, 2 and 3 City Place.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Beehive1_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beehive1-104">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Beehive2_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beehive2-105">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Beehive3_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beehive3-106">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The complex was developed by BAA Lynton.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> A number of airlines have had offices at the Beehive, including <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Helicopters" title="British Airways Helicopters">BEA/British Airways Helicopters</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-BAH_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BAH-108">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jersey_Airlines" title="Jersey Airlines">Jersey Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caledonian_Airways" title="Caledonian Airways">Caledonian Airways</a>, Virgin Atlantic and <a href="/wiki/GB_Airways" title="GB Airways">GB Airways</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GB_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GB-110">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jersey_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jersey-111">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Caledonian_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caledonian-112">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Virgin_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Virgin-113">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\nOther airlines which had headquarters on airport property (including office buildings on the site of, or adjacent to, the original 1930s airport) include <a href="/wiki/British_Caledonian" title="British Caledonian">British Caledonian</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/British_United_Airways" title="British United Airways">British United Airways</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/CityFlyer_Express" title="CityFlyer Express">CityFlyer Express</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fastjet" title="Fastjet">Fastjet</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Laker_Airways" title="Laker Airways">Laker Airways</a><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tradewinds_Airways" title="Tradewinds Airways">Tradewinds Airways</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-flight1969_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight1969-120">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gatwick_Aviation_Museum">Gatwick Aviation Museum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Gatwick Aviation Museum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Aviation_Museum" title="Gatwick Aviation Museum">Gatwick Aviation Museum</a></div>\n<p>Situated to the north-west of the airfield near the village of <a href="/wiki/Charlwood" title="Charlwood">Charlwood</a>, there is a museum including original items and photographs from Gatwick\'s history, as well as a variety of military aircraft.  It is open Friday, Saturday and Sunday all year round.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gatwick_South_Terminal_international_arrivals_concourse.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Passengers with luggage looking at arriving-flights board" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Gatwick_South_Terminal_international_arrivals_concourse.JPG/220px-Gatwick_South_Terminal_international_arrivals_concourse.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Gatwick_South_Terminal_international_arrivals_concourse.JPG/330px-Gatwick_South_Terminal_international_arrivals_concourse.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Gatwick_South_Terminal_international_arrivals_concourse.JPG/440px-Gatwick_South_Terminal_international_arrivals_concourse.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3296" data-file-height="2472" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gatwick_South_Terminal_international_arrivals_concourse.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>South Terminal international arrivals concourse</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gatwick_Airport_North_Terminal_shuttle_transit_arrival_platform_look_north.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Gatwick_Airport_North_Terminal_shuttle_transit_arrival_platform_look_north.jpg/220px-Gatwick_Airport_North_Terminal_shuttle_transit_arrival_platform_look_north.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Gatwick_Airport_North_Terminal_shuttle_transit_arrival_platform_look_north.jpg/330px-Gatwick_Airport_North_Terminal_shuttle_transit_arrival_platform_look_north.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Gatwick_Airport_North_Terminal_shuttle_transit_arrival_platform_look_north.jpg/440px-Gatwick_Airport_North_Terminal_shuttle_transit_arrival_platform_look_north.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gatwick_Airport_North_Terminal_shuttle_transit_arrival_platform_look_north.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gatwick\'s North Terminal transit station after renovation</div></div></div>\n<p>The airport has two terminals, South and North. Both have shops and restaurants landside and airside, and all areas are accessible to disabled passengers. There are facilities for baby changing and feeding. Business travellers have specialised lounges. The North and South Terminals are connected by a 0.75-mile (1.21&#160;km), elevated, two-way automated <a href="/wiki/People_mover" title="People mover">people mover</a> landside. They are not connected once past security.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Terminal">South Terminal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: South Terminal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The official opening of the central and main pier of what is now the South Terminal, with 11 aircraft stands, was on 9 June 1958. Gatwick was one of the world\'s first airports with an enclosed <a href="/wiki/Pier_(architecture)" title="Pier (architecture)">pier</a>-based terminal, which allowed passengers to walk under cover to waiting areas near the aircraft (with only a short walk outdoors).<sup id="cite_ref-Gatwick_History_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gatwick_History-123">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Another feature of Gatwick\'s new air terminal was its <a href="/wiki/Modular_design" title="Modular design">modular design</a>, permitting subsequent, phased expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-GoldenGatwick_8_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GoldenGatwick_8-124">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As passenger numbers grew, a circular satellite pier was added to the terminal building. It was connected to the main terminal by the UK\'s first automated <a href="/wiki/People_mover" title="People mover">people mover</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-Gatwick_History_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gatwick_History-123">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> This replaced the original North pier dating from 1962; and the people mover was subsequently replaced with a walkway and <a href="/wiki/Moving_walkway" title="Moving walkway">travelators</a>.\n</p><p>As of June 2020, the South Terminal has been temporarily closed, and all airlines normally operating from this terminal have been relocated to the North Terminal, owing to the sharp decline in passenger traffic as a result of the devastating impact of the COVID-19 pandemic. <sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Terminal">North Terminal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: North Terminal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Construction began on the North Terminal on land previously earmarked for a second runway in the draft plan of May 1970. This was the largest construction project south of London in the 1980s, costing \xc2\xa3200&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-runway_moratorium_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-runway_moratorium-52">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-1979_expansion_plans_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1979_expansion_plans-53">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> In 1991 a second aircraft pier was added to the North Terminal.\n</p><p>On 16 May 2005 the new Pier 6 opened at a cost of \xc2\xa3110&#160;million, adding 11 pier-served aircraft stands. The pier is linked to the North Terminal\'s main building by the largest air passenger bridge in the world, spanning a taxiway and providing passengers with views of the airport and taxiing aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A large extension to the terminal was opened by former Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/John_Major" title="John Major">John Major</a> in November 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_assignments_and_rearrangements">Terminal assignments and rearrangements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Terminal assignments and rearrangements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As part of a seven-year strategic commercial partnership between Gatwick and <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a>, the airport proposed a number of changes to individual airlines\' terminal locations. These would see EasyJet consolidate all its Gatwick operations in the North Terminal, while <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">Virgin Atlantic</a> would swap their terminals. Gatwick believes that these terminal moves improve the airport\'s operational efficiency and resilience, as the use of different terminals by EasyJet and British Airways reduces pressure on the North Terminal\'s check-in, security, boarding and <a href="/wiki/Airport_ramp" class="mw-redirect" title="Airport ramp">ramp</a> areas at peak times. In addition, a terminal swap by Virgin frees up lounge and gate space for BA long-haul passengers in the South Terminal and, unlike BA\'s current short-haul schedules, Virgin\'s long-haul schedules do not clash with EasyJet\'s busy schedule in the North Terminal due to the airlines\' differing peak times.<sup id="cite_ref-EZY_LGW_Takeover_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EZY_LGW_Takeover-69">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It was confirmed in January 2015 that British Airways would move all its flights to the South Terminal in November 2016 while all EasyJet flights will be consolidated in the North Terminal at the same time.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EZY_LGW_TerminalConsolidation_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EZY_LGW_TerminalConsolidation-68">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> However it was decided in February 2016 to postpone the agreed relocation of airlines until 25 January 2017, to avoid operational disruptions over the 2016\xe2\x80\x9317 Christmas season and to give all parties involved enough time to deal with any unforeseen issues ahead of the <a href="/wiki/English_school_holidays" title="English school holidays">February 2017 half-term holidays</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> The relocation of these airlines was accomplished by the revised date on 25 January 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span International Airport">Malta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Airport" title="Sofia Airport">Sofia</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Traffic_and_statistics">Traffic and statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Traffic and statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2015, Gatwick became the first single-runway airport to handle more than 40&#160;million passengers annually.<sup id="cite_ref-GAL_2015Stats_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GAL_2015Stats-158">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> By 2016, <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a> accounted for over 40% of Gatwick\'s total passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LGW_Nos_2016_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGW_Nos_2016-74">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> When ranked by <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s busiest airports by passenger traffic">global passenger traffic</a>, Gatwick is 35th busiest internationally and the eighth <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">busiest airport in Europe</a>. Gatwick is the world\'s leading <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost</a> airport<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> and until March 2017 had the world\'s busiest single-use runway,<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;nb 9&#93;</a></sup> with a maximum of 55 aircraft movements per hour.<sup id="cite_ref-FutureofBAA_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FutureofBAA-162">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Times_of_India_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times_of_India-163">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Busiest_routes">Busiest routes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Traffic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1017906329">@media all and (max-width:720px){body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .mw-graph{min-width:100%!important;max-width:100%;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:visible}}.mw-parser-output .mw-graph-img{width:inherit;height:inherit}</style><div class="mw-graph mw-graph-always mw-graph-nofallback" style="min-width:540px;min-height:300px" data-graph-id="511586a2ca0b05512fd01a637d9a694854920869"></div>\n<p><small>See <a class="external text" href="https://query.wikidata.org/embed.html#%23%20Scroll%20down%20and%20hit%20blue%20arrow%20down%20to%20run%20and%20see%20the%20results%20%2B%20the%20sources%0ASELECT%20%3Fyear%20%3Fitem%20%3FitemLabel%20%28MAX%28%3Fnumber%29%20AS%20%3Fpassengers%29%0A%20%20%28SAMPLE%28COALESCE%28%3Freference_URL%2C%20%3Fmonthly_reference_URL2%29%29%20AS%20%3Fsample_reference_URL%29%0AWITH%0A%7B%0A%20%20SELECT%20%3Fitem%20%3Fstatement%20%3Fdate%20%3Fyear%20%3Ftimevalue%20%3Fnumberperperiod%20%3Freference_URL%0A%20%20WHERE%0A%20%20%7B%0A%20%20%20%20%3Fitem%20wdt%3AP238%20%3Fairport_code%0A%20%20%20%20VALUES%20%3Fairport_code%20%0A%20%20%20%20%7B%0A%20%22LGW%22%0A%20%20%20%20%7D%0A%20%20%20%20%3Fitem%20p%3AP3872%20%3Fstatement.%0A%20%20%20%20%3Fstatement%20pqv%3AP585%20%3Ftimevalue%3B%0A%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20ps%3AP3872%20%3Fnumberperperiod.%0A%20%20%20%20%3Ftimevalue%20wikibase%3AtimeValue%20%3Fdate.%0A%20%20%20%20OPTIONAL%20%7B%20%3Fstatement%20pq%3AP518%20%3Fapplies.%20%7D%0A%20%20%20%20OPTIONAL%20%7B%20%3Fstatement%20prov%3AwasDerivedFrom%20%2F%20%28pr%3AP854%7Cpr%3AP4656%29%20%3Freference_URL.%20%7D%0A%20%20%20%20FILTER%20%28BOUND%28%3Fapplies%29%3Dfalse%20%7C%7C%20%3Fapplies%20%3D%20wd%3AQ2165236%20%29%0A%20%20%20%20MINUS%20%7B%20%3Fstatement%20wikibase%3Arank%20wikibase%3ADeprecatedRank%20%7D%0A%20%20%20%20BIND%20%28YEAR%28%3Fdate%29%20AS%20%3Fyear%29%0A%20%20%20%20FILTER%20%28%3Fyear%20%3E1949%29.%0A%20%20%20%20FILTER%20%28%3Fyear%20%3C%20YEAR%28NOW%28%29%29%29%0A%20%20%7D%0A%7D%20AS%20%25airport%0AWHERE%0A%7B%0A%20%20%7B%0A%20%20%20%20%23%20Get%20the%20sum%20of%20monthly%20values%20within%20a%20year%0A%20%20%20%20SELECT%20%3Fitem%20%3Fyear%20%28SUM%28%3Fmax_numberperperiod%29%20AS%20%3Fnumber%29%20%28SAMPLE%28%3Fmonthly_reference_URL%29%20AS%20%3Fmonthly_reference_URL2%29%0A%20%20%20%20WHERE%0A%20%20%20%20%7B%0A%20%20%20%20%20%20%23%20Get%20the%20maximal%20value%20and%20a%20sample%20reference%20URL%20for%20each%20unique%20month%0A%20%20%20%20%20%20%7B%0A%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20SELECT%20%3Fitem%20%3Fyear%20%28MAX%28%3Fnumberperperiod%29%20AS%20%3Fmax_numberperperiod%29%20%28SAMPLE%28%3Freference_URL%29%20AS%20%3Fmonthly_reference_URL%29%0A%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20WHERE%0A%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%7B%0A%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20INCLUDE%20%25airport%0A%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%3Ftimevalue%20wikibase%3AtimePrecision%20%3Fprec.%0A%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20FILTER%20%28%3Fprec%20%3E%209%29%23%20precision%20more%20precise%20or%20equal%20to%20month%0A%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%7D%0A%20%20%20%20%20%20%20%20GROUP%20BY%20%3Fitem%20%3Fyear%20%3Fdate%0A%20%20%20%20%20%20%7D%0A%20%20%20%20%7D%0A%20%20%20%20GROUP%20BY%20%3Fitem%20%3Fyear%0A%20%20%7D%0A%20%20UNION%0A%20%20%7B%0A%20%20%20%20%3Ftimevalue%20wikibase%3AtimePrecision%209%20.%0A%20%20%20%20BIND%20%28%3Fnumberperperiod%20AS%20%3Fnumber%29%0A%20%20%20%20BIND%20%28%3Freference_URL%20AS%20%3Fsample_reference_URL%29%0A%20%20%20%20INCLUDE%20%25airport%0A%20%20%7D%0A%20%20SERVICE%20wikibase%3Alabel%20%7B%20bd%3AserviceParam%20wikibase%3Alanguage%20%22en%22.%20%7D%0A%7D%0AGROUP%20BY%20%3Fitem%20%3FitemLabel%20%3Fyear%0AORDER%20BY%20%3Fitem%20DESC%20%28%3Fyear%29">source Wikidata query and sources</a>.</small>\n</p><p>Gatwick handled 186,172 passengers during its first seven months of operation after the 1956\xe2\x80\x9358 reconstruction; the annual number of passengers passing through the airport was 368,000 in 1959 and 470,000 in 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-Gatwick_History_123-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gatwick_History-123">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GoldenGatwick_9_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GoldenGatwick_9-165">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\nPassenger numbers reached one&#160;million for the first time during the 1962\xe2\x80\x9363 fiscal year,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;nb 10&#93;</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/British_United_Airways" title="British United Airways">British United Airways</a> (BUA) accounting for four-fifths.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> The 1.5&#160;million mark was exceeded for the first time during the 1966\xe2\x80\x9367 fiscal year.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;nb 11&#93;</a></sup> This was also the first time more than half a million scheduled passengers used the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Gatwick accommodated two&#160;million passengers for the first time during the 1967\xe2\x80\x9368 fiscal year<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;nb 12&#93;</a></sup> and three&#160;million in the 1969\xe2\x80\x9370 fiscal year,<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;nb 13&#93;</a></sup> with BUA accounting for nearly half.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> By the early 1970s, 5&#160;million passengers used Gatwick each year, with a record 5.7&#160;million during the 1973\xe2\x80\x9374 fiscal year.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;nb 14&#93;</a></sup> During that period, <a href="/wiki/British_Caledonian" title="British Caledonian">British Caledonian</a> accounted for approximately half of all charter passengers and three-fourths of scheduled passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-GoldenGatwick_10_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GoldenGatwick_10-175">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Within a decade annual passenger numbers doubled, to 10&#160;million; they doubled again, to over 20&#160;million, by the late 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-Gatwick_History_123-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gatwick_History-123">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Express2_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Express2-176">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-..._Bloomers_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-..._Bloomers-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-..._up_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-..._up-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> By the turn of the millennium, Gatwick handled more than 30&#160;million passengers annually.<sup id="cite_ref-Gatwick_History_123-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gatwick_History-123">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:right; data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /><span
