srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /><span style="visibility:hidden;color:transparent;">0</span>78.2%</td>\n<td>79,489</td>\n<td>TBA\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="5" style="text-align:right;"><sup><i>Source 2000\xe2\x80\x932016: <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Civil_Aviation_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Civil Aviation Authority">UK Civil Aviation Authority</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup></sup><br /><sup><i>Source 2017: Gatwick Airport Limited</i><sup id="cite_ref-LGW_2017_GAL_Stats_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGW_2017_GAL_Stats-180">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>46.1&#160;million passengers passed through Gatwick in 2018, an increase of 1.1% over the previous year. <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">North Atlantic</a> and other long-haul<sup id="cite_ref-north_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-north-181">&#91;nb 17&#93;</a></sup> traffic recorded increases over the previous year of 24.4% and 12.7% to 4.04&#160;million and 4.65&#160;million passengers, respectively. UK,<sup id="cite_ref-channel_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-channel-182">&#91;nb 18&#93;</a></sup> European charter,<sup id="cite_ref-NorthAfrica_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorthAfrica-183">&#91;nb 19&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Irish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> scheduled passenger traffic recorded decreases over the previous year of 8.7%, 5.7%, 1.1% and 0.9% to 3.73&#160;million, 2.88&#160;million, 1.67&#160;million and 29.11&#160;million, respectively. Air transport movements decreased by 0.7% to 283,926. Cargo volume increased by 16.1% to 112,676 metric tonnes.<sup id="cite_ref-LGW_2018_GAL_Stats_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGW_2018_GAL_Stats-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Compared with a year earlier, January to March 2019 passenger numbers increased by 4% to 9.675&#160;million (an increase of 374,700 over January to March 2018). The following changes were recorded amongst individual passenger traffic categories: North Atlantic traffic +15.3% (784,200 passengers); European scheduled traffic +3.9% (5.649&#160;million passengers); other long-haul<sup id="cite_ref-north_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-north-181">&#91;nb 17&#93;</a></sup> traffic +3.2% (1.277&#160;million passengers); European charter<sup id="cite_ref-NorthAfrica_183-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorthAfrica-183">&#91;nb 19&#93;</a></sup> traffic +2.1% (710,900 passengers); Irish traffic +1.6% (412,000 passengers) and UK<sup id="cite_ref-channel_182-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-channel-182">&#91;nb 18&#93;</a></sup> traffic -0.2% (841,700 passengers). Air transport movements increased by 3.3% to 62,392. Cargo volume increased by 7.2% to 27,390 metric tonnes, which was driven by a 7.5% increase in overall long-haul passenger traffic. The growing popularity of the GatwickConnects flight connections assistance service provided by the airport for self-connecting passengers was driven by additional passengers changing flights at Gatwick whose journey originated in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> (+80%), <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a> (+58%) and <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a> (+50%).<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transport">Ground transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Ground transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gatwick_North_Terminal_121.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Grassy median, with billboard and road sign" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Gatwick_North_Terminal_121.JPG/220px-Gatwick_North_Terminal_121.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Gatwick_North_Terminal_121.JPG/330px-Gatwick_North_Terminal_121.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Gatwick_North_Terminal_121.JPG/440px-Gatwick_North_Terminal_121.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3296" data-file-height="2472" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gatwick_North_Terminal_121.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>North Terminal <a href="/wiki/A23_road" title="A23 road">A23</a> roundabout</div></div></div>\n<p>Gatwick has set goals of 40% public transport use by the time annual passenger traffic reaches 40&#160;million (in 2015) and 45% by the time it reaches 45&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport is accessible from a motorway <a href="/wiki/Spur_route" title="Spur route">spur road</a> at junction 9A of the <a href="/wiki/M23_motorway" title="M23 motorway">M23</a>, which links to the main M23 motorway 1 mile (1.6&#160;km) east at junction 9. The M23 connects with London\'s <a href="/wiki/Beltway" class="mw-redirect" title="Beltway">orbital motorway</a>, the <a href="/wiki/M25_motorway" title="M25 motorway">M25</a>, 9 miles (14&#160;km) north; this provides access to much of <a href="/wiki/Greater_London" title="Greater London">Greater London</a>, the <a href="/wiki/South_East_England" title="South East England">South East</a> and beyond, and the M23 is the main route for traffic to the airport. Gatwick is also accessible from the <a href="/wiki/A23_road" title="A23 road">A23</a>, which serves <a href="/wiki/Horley" title="Horley">Horley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Redhill,_Surrey" title="Redhill, Surrey">Redhill</a> to the north and <a href="/wiki/Crawley" title="Crawley">Crawley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brighton" title="Brighton">Brighton</a> to the south. The <a href="/wiki/A217_road" title="A217 road">A217</a> provides access northwards to the town of <a href="/wiki/Reigate" title="Reigate">Reigate</a>. The airport has long- and short-stay car parks at the airport and off-site, although these are often full in summer. Local restrictions limit parking at (and near) Gatwick.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gatwick_Airport_Station_02.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Outdoor station with enclosed, overhead walkway" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Gatwick_Airport_Station_02.JPG/220px-Gatwick_Airport_Station_02.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Gatwick_Airport_Station_02.JPG/330px-Gatwick_Airport_Station_02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Gatwick_Airport_Station_02.JPG/440px-Gatwick_Airport_Station_02.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gatwick_Airport_Station_02.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport_railway_station" title="Gatwick Airport railway station">Gatwick Airport railway station</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport_railway_station" title="Gatwick Airport railway station">Gatwick Airport railway station</a></div>\n<p>The airport railway station, which is next to the South Terminal, provides connections along the <a href="/wiki/Brighton_Main_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Brighton Main Line">Brighton Main Line</a> and Thameslink Core to <a href="/wiki/London_Victoria_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London Victoria railway station">Victoria</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Bridge_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London Bridge railway station">London Bridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_railway_station" title="St Pancras railway station">St Pancras</a> stations in London and <a href="/wiki/Brighton_railway_station" title="Brighton railway station">Brighton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Worthing_railway_station" title="Worthing railway station">Worthing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastbourne_railway_station" title="Eastbourne railway station">Eastbourne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Harbour_railway_station" title="Portsmouth Harbour railway station">Portsmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chichester_railway_station" title="Chichester railway station">Chichester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bognor_Regis_railway_station" title="Bognor Regis railway station">Bognor Regis</a> to the south. Although the <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Express" title="Gatwick Express">Gatwick Express</a> to Victoria is the best-known service from the station, other companies (including <a href="/wiki/Govia_Thameslink_Railway" title="Govia Thameslink Railway">Thameslink</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Railway_(train_operating_company)" title="Great Western Railway (train operating company)">Great Western Railway</a>) also use the station and Southern services Victoria and London Bridge under its own name. Thameslink provides direct trains to <a href="/wiki/Luton_Airport_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Luton Airport railway station">Luton Airport</a>; Great Western Railway trains directly link Gatwick Airport with <a href="/wiki/Guildford_railway_station" title="Guildford railway station">Guildford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reading_railway_station" title="Reading railway station">Reading</a> for onwards connections to <a href="/wiki/Oxford_railway_station" title="Oxford railway station">Oxford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Temple_Meads_railway_station" title="Bristol Temple Meads railway station">Bristol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_railway_station" title="Plymouth railway station">Plymouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Central_railway_station" title="Cardiff Central railway station">Cardiff</a>. Pedestrians may reach <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a> by a <a href="/wiki/London_Buses_route_X26" title="London Buses route X26">X26 Express bus</a> from outside <a href="/wiki/East_Croydon_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="East Croydon railway station">East Croydon station</a>, an intermediate stop for rail service to London.\n</p><p>London <a href="/wiki/Oyster_Cards" class="mw-redirect" title="Oyster Cards">Oyster Cards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contactless_payment" title="Contactless payment">contactless cards</a> have been accepted on all rail routes from Gatwick Airport into London<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> since January 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus"><span class="anchor" id="Bus_and_coach"></span>Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/National_Express_Coaches" title="National Express Coaches">National Express Coaches</a> operates coaches to <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Stansted_Airport" title="London Stansted Airport">Stansted Airport</a> and cities and towns throughout the region and country. <a href="/wiki/Oxford_Bus_Company" title="Oxford Bus Company">Oxford Bus Company</a> operates direct services to <a href="/wiki/Oxford" title="Oxford">Oxford</a>, and <a href="/wiki/EasyBus" title="EasyBus">EasyBus</a> operates mini-coaches from both terminals to <a href="/wiki/Earls_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="Earls Court">Earls Court</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Brompton" title="West Brompton">West Brompton</a>.\n</p><p>Local buses connect the North and South Terminals with <a href="/wiki/Crawley" title="Crawley">Crawley</a>, Horley, Redhill, <a href="/wiki/Horsham" title="Horsham">Horsham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caterham" title="Caterham">Caterham</a>. Services are offered by <a href="/wiki/Metrobus_(South_East_England)" title="Metrobus (South East England)">Metrobus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crawley_Fastway" class="mw-redirect" title="Crawley Fastway">Fastway</a>, a partly guided <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">bus rapid transit</a> system which was the first of its kind to be built outside a major city.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bicycle"><span class="anchor" id="Cycle"></span>Bicycle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Bicycle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/National_Cycle_Route_21" title="National Cycle Route 21">Route 21</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Cycle_Network" title="National Cycle Network">National Cycle Network</a> passes under South Terminal, allowing virtually traffic-free cycling and walking northwards to Horley and southwards to <a href="/wiki/Three_Bridges" title="Three Bridges">Three Bridges</a> and Crawley. A goods-style lift runs between the terminal and ground level (labelled "Lift to Cycle Route"), near Zone L.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_transfer">Terminal transfer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Terminal transfer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shuttle_train_at_Gatwick_North_Terminal_(geograph_3996833).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Shuttle_train_at_Gatwick_North_Terminal_%28geograph_3996833%29.jpg/220px-Shuttle_train_at_Gatwick_North_Terminal_%28geograph_3996833%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Shuttle_train_at_Gatwick_North_Terminal_%28geograph_3996833%29.jpg/330px-Shuttle_train_at_Gatwick_North_Terminal_%28geograph_3996833%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Shuttle_train_at_Gatwick_North_Terminal_%28geograph_3996833%29.jpg/440px-Shuttle_train_at_Gatwick_North_Terminal_%28geograph_3996833%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shuttle_train_at_Gatwick_North_Terminal_(geograph_3996833).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The inter-terminal transit</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport_Shuttle_Transit" title="Gatwick Airport Shuttle Transit">Gatwick Airport Shuttle Transit</a></div>\n<p>The airport\'s North and South Terminals are connected by a 0.75 miles (1.21&#160;km), elevated, two-way <a href="/wiki/Automated_people_mover" class="mw-redirect" title="Automated people mover">automated people mover</a> track. The transit shuttle normally consists of two automatic, three-car, driver-less trains. Although colloquially known as a "<a href="/wiki/Monorail" title="Monorail">monorail</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-hudson_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hudson-188">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> the shuttle instead runs on a dual, concrete track with rubber tyres. The transit is ground-side, and besides linking the two terminals also serves to link the North terminal to the airport railway station.\n</p><p>The shuttle opened in 1987, along with the North Terminal, and initially used <a href="/wiki/Adtranz_C-100" title="Adtranz C-100">Adtranz C-100</a> people-mover cars which remained in operation until September 2009, by which time they had travelled a total of 2.5&#160;million miles (4&#160;million km). Gatwick began upgrading its shuttle service in April 2008, with a bus replacement service in place from September 2009. A new operating system and shuttle cars (six <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_CX-100" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombardier CX-100">Bombardier CX-100</a> vehicles)<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> was installed, and the guideway and transit stations were refurbished at a total cost of \xc2\xa345&#160;million. The system re-opened on 1 July 2010, two months ahead of schedule;<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> it featured live journey information and sensory technology to count the number of passengers at stations.\n</p><p>An earlier transit system, that opened in 1983 to link the main terminal (now the South Terminal) to the (then new) circular satellite pier, was the UK\'s first automated people-moving system. This system has since been replaced by a walkway-and-<a href="/wiki/Moving_walkway" title="Moving walkway">moving walkway</a> link, although the remains of the elevated guideway are still visible.<sup id="cite_ref-hudson_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hudson-188">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_proposals"><span class="anchor" id="Proposals_for_expansion"></span>Expansion proposals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Expansion proposals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Expansion_of_Gatwick_Airport" title="Expansion of Gatwick Airport">Expansion of Gatwick Airport</a></div>\n<p>Gatwick has been included in a number of reviews of airport capacity in southeastern England. Expansion options have included a third terminal and a second runway, although a 40-year agreement not to build a second runway was made in 1979 with <a href="/wiki/West_Sussex_County_Council" title="West Sussex County Council">West Sussex County Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-runway_moratorium_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-runway_moratorium-52">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-1979_expansion_plans_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1979_expansion_plans-53">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Expanded operations would allow Gatwick to handle more passengers than Heathrow does today, with a new terminal between two wide-spaced runways. This would complement or replace the South Terminal, depending on expected future traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-LGW_Interim_Master_Plan_2006_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGW_Interim_Master_Plan_2006-193">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Airport management\'s proposal for a second runway (south of the existing runway and airport boundary) was unveiled in July 2013. This was shortlisted for further consideration by the <a href="/wiki/Airports_Commission" title="Airports Commission">Airports Commission</a> in December 2013, and the commission\'s final report was published in July 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-LGW_2nd_runway_proposals_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGW_2nd_runway_proposals-194">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Another proposal would extend the North Terminal south, with a passenger bridge in the area currently occupied by aircraft stands without <a href="/wiki/Jet_bridge" title="Jet bridge">jet bridges</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LGW_Interim_Master_Plan_2006_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGW_Interim_Master_Plan_2006-193">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Gatwick\'s draft master plan (released for consultation on 13 October 2011) apparently dropped the passenger-bridge plan in favour of a mid-field satellite (next to the control tower) linking to the North Terminal as part of an expanded 2030 single-runway, two-terminal airport.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In late 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a> (DfT) also began a feasibility study for a high-speed rail link between Gatwick and Heathrow as part of a plan combining the airports into a "collective" or "virtual hub", <a href="/wiki/Heathwick" title="Heathwick">Heathwick</a>. The scheme envisages a high-speed rail route parallel to the <a href="/wiki/M25_motorway" title="M25 motorway">M25</a>, covering 35 miles (56&#160;km) in 15 minutes. Trains would reach speeds of 180&#160;mph (290&#160;km/h), and passengers would need to pass through immigration (or check in) only once. A 2018 proposal for a high-speed railway link to Heathrow, <a href="/wiki/HS4Air" title="HS4Air">HS4Air</a>, is currently being considered by the DfT. The proposal is part of a scheme to link the <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_1" title="High Speed 1">High Speed 1</a> and <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_2" title="High Speed 2">High Speed 2</a> railway lines and connect regional cities in Britain to the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tute_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tute-197">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> The DfT will respond to the HS4Air plans in the autumn of 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-es-220718_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-es-220718-199">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 July 2015, the Airports Commission submitted their final report, recommending the expansion of Heathrow Airport as opposed to Gatwick. Whilst the commission recognised Gatwick\'s benefits and relatively less environmental consequences than Heathrow, they felt the economic benefits of Gatwick vs. Heathrow were not as great, nor as broad-ranging.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> Gatwick disputed the findings.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>15 September 1936 \xe2\x80\x93 A <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Ltd_(1935%E2%80%9339)" class="mw-redirect" title="British Airways Ltd (1935\xe2\x80\x9339)">British Airways Ltd</a> <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Express" title="De Havilland Express">de Havilland DH 86</a> on a night mail flight to <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> crashed on takeoff, killing the airline\'s chief pilot and two crew members.<sup id="cite_ref-September1936Crash1_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-September1936Crash1-202">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-September1936Crash2_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-September1936Crash2-203">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>November 1936 \xe2\x80\x93 A <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Ltd_(1935%E2%80%9339)" class="mw-redirect" title="British Airways Ltd (1935\xe2\x80\x9339)">British Airways Ltd</a> <a href="/wiki/Fokker_F.XII" title="Fokker F.XII">Fokker F 12</a> crashed in a wood 4.5 miles (7.2&#160;km) south of Gatwick on its <a href="/wiki/Final_approach_(aviation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Final approach (aviation)">final approach</a> to the airport under a low <a href="/wiki/Ceiling_(cloud)" title="Ceiling (cloud)">ceiling</a> in poor visibility, killing both pilots and seriously injuring the <a href="/wiki/Flight_engineer" title="Flight engineer">flight engineer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-November1936Crash_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-November1936Crash-204">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>17 February 1959 \xe2\x80\x93 A <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">Turkish Airlines</a> <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount_variants#Viscount_700" title="Vickers Viscount variants">Vickers Viscount 794D</a> (registration: TC-SEV) on an <a href="/wiki/1959_Turkish_Airlines_Gatwick_crash" title="1959 Turkish Airlines Gatwick crash">international charter flight</a> crashed in heavy fog at <a href="/wiki/Newdigate" title="Newdigate">Newdigate</a>, Surrey, on its approach to Gatwick after striking trees. Fourteen of the 24 on board died, and Turkish Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Adnan_Menderes" title="Adnan Menderes">Adnan Menderes</a> was amongst the survivors.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Incidents_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Incidents-206">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>5 January 1969 \xe2\x80\x93 A <a href="/wiki/Boeing_727-100C" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 727-100C">Boeing 727-113C</a> (registration: YA-FAR) operating <a href="/wiki/Ariana_Afghan_Airlines_Flight_701" title="Ariana Afghan Airlines Flight 701">flight 701</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ariana_Afghan_Airlines" title="Ariana Afghan Airlines">Ariana Afghan Airlines</a> arriving from <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a>, Germany, crashed into a house in <a href="/wiki/Fernhill,_West_Sussex" title="Fernhill, West Sussex">Fernhill</a> (near <a href="/wiki/Horley" title="Horley">Horley</a>, Surrey) in low visibility. The flaps were not extended to maintain flight at final-approach speed. Forty-eight of the 62 on board died, in addition to two on the ground.<sup id="cite_ref-Incidents_206-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Incidents-206">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>28 January 1972 \xe2\x80\x93 A <a href="/wiki/British_Caledonian" title="British Caledonian">British Caledonian</a> <a href="/wiki/Vickers_VC10" title="Vickers VC10">Vickers VC10-1109</a> (registration: G-ARTA) with no passengers aboard sustained severe structural damage as a result of a <a href="/wiki/Hard_landing" title="Hard landing">hard landing</a> at Gatwick at the end of a short ferry flight from Heathrow, where the aircraft had been diverted due to fog at Gatwick. After touching down on runway 08 and applying <a href="/wiki/Spoiler_(aeronautics)" title="Spoiler (aeronautics)">spoilers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thrust_reversal" title="Thrust reversal">reverse thrust</a>, the aircraft became airborne again, bounced twice and landed heavily. This resulted in a burst front wheel tyre, a separated wheel and a crumpled fuselage (immediately in front of and behind the wings).<sup id="cite_ref-Woodley_60_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Woodley_60-211">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> A survey of the aircraft\'s damage revealed that its <a href="/wiki/Airframe" title="Airframe">airframe</a> was bent out of shape, requiring extensive repairs to be restored to <a href="/wiki/Airworthiness" title="Airworthiness">airworthiness</a>. Since the repairs were not cost-effective, the airline\'s management decided to <a href="/wiki/Cannibalization_(parts)" title="Cannibalization (parts)">cannibalise</a> the aircraft for spare parts before scrapping it at Gatwick in 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>20 July 1975 \xe2\x80\x93 A <a href="/wiki/British_Island_Airways" title="British Island Airways">British Island Airways</a> (BIA) <a href="/wiki/Handley_Page_Dart_Herald#Specifications_(Dart_Herald_200)" title="Handley Page Dart Herald">Handley Page Dart Herald 201</a> (registration: G-APWF) was involved in a runway accident while departing on a scheduled flight to Guernsey. The aircraft lifted off from runway 26 after a ground run of 2,490 feet (760&#160;m), and appeared airborne for 411&#160;ft (125&#160;m) (with its landing gear retracting), before the rear underside of the fuselage settled back onto the runway and brought the aircraft to a stop. An investigation concluded that the landing gear was retracted before the aircraft had become established in a climb and the flap setting and takeoff speed were incorrect. Although the aircraft incurred substantial damage, none of the 45 occupants were hurt.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>19\xe2\x80\x9321 December 2018 \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport_drone_incident" title="Gatwick Airport drone incident">Major disruption to the airport</a> was caused by a <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">drone</a> flying near the runway, which was shut for about six hours on the 19th. The airport reopened at 03:01 the next morning until another sighting forced it to close again about 45 minutes later. As of 00:15 on the 21st, the airport was still closed with about 110,000 passengers and 760 flights affected.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Officials called the drone flying a "deliberate act of disruption", but did not classify it as terrorism.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Drone_Dec_2018_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Drone_Dec_2018-216">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> The army were deployed to assist police in ending the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-46623754_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-46623754-217">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> The runway reopened with limited capacity at around 06:00 on the 21st.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> There was another suspension of flights from 17:10 to 18:23 on the 21st. Later that day a man and a woman were arrested in connection with the incident;<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> they were released without charge on 23 December with Sussex Police saying that they "are no longer suspects".<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph2312_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph2312-221">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On February 26, 2020 a <a href="/wiki/Titan_Airways" title="Titan Airways">Titan Airways</a> <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320">Airbus A321-211</a> suffered an engine fire immediately after takeoff. Shortly after the other engine surged and stalled. The aircraft landed safely at Gatwick eleven minutes after takeoff. The <a href="/wiki/Air_Accidents_Investigation_Branch" title="Air Accidents Investigation Branch">Air Accidents Investigation Branch</a> determined <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fuel_contamination&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fuel contamination (page does not exist)">fuel contamination</a> following defective maintenance had gone undetected for two days and caused the incident. Safety recommendations were made to the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Aviation_Safety_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="European Union Aviation Safety Agency">European Union Aviation Safety Agency</a>, and changes made by organisations including <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association" title="International Air Transport Association">International Air Transport Association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gatwick_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section:
